# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Request Header Injection Validation

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that sanitize or validate HTTP request headers to prevent header injection: the header validation logic, the forbidden header list enforcement, and the internal header stripping.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of HTTP request header injection validation in Envoy v1.31.2. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I identified **22 C++ source files** across Envoy that implement header injection prevention:

### Core Validation Layer
- **Header Map** (`envoy/http/header_map.h`): Base validation for embedded control characters
- **Header Utility** (`source/common/http/header_utility.cc`): Core functions like `headerNameIsValid()`, `headerValueIsValid()`, `checkValidRequestHeaders()`
- **Connection Manager Utility** (`source/common/http/conn_manager_utility.cc`): Internal header stripping for edge requests, TE header sanitization

### Protocol-Specific Validators
- **HTTP/1.1 Codec** (`source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc`): Connection header sanitization
- **HTTP/2 Codec** (`source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.cc`): Header validation during parsing
- **HTTP/1 Validator** (`source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http1_header_validator.cc`): Content-length sanitization, path validation
- **HTTP/2 Validator** (`source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http2_header_validator.cc`): Forbidden header enforcement (connection, upgrade, keep-alive, proxy-connection, transfer-encoding)
- **QUIC/HTTP3** (`source/common/quic/`): Per-header validation for QUIC streams

### Key Security Features
1. **Forbidden Header List**: HTTP/2 strictly rejects connection-specific headers
2. **Internal Header Stripping**: Removes x-envoy-* headers from untrusted clients
3. **Connection Header Sanitization**: Prevents header injection via nominated headers
4. **Path Validation**: RFC 3986 compliance with null byte and fragment stripping
5. **Underscore Handling**: Configurable rejection/dropping of headers with undersc

(source/common/http/utility.cc)**\\n- `sanitizeConnectionHeader()`: Prevents header injection via the Connection header by:\\n  - Limiting nominated headers to 10 maximum (prevents DOS)\\n  - Removing headers nominated by the Connection header\\n  - Rejecting if Connection nominates x-forwarded-* headers or pseudo-headers (RFC violation)\\n  - Sanitizing the TE (Transfer-Encoding) header when nominated\\n  - Validating TE values do not exceed 256 bytes\\n  - Validates nominated headers conform to HTTP hop-by-hop semantics\\n\\n### HTTP/1.1 Specific Validation\\n\\n**Header Codec Validation (source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc)**\\n- Validates header values for invalid characters using `headerValueIsValid()`\\n- Checks header names and values conform to HTTP/1.1 semantics\\n- characters)\\n\\n**HTTP/1 Header Validator (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http1_header_validator.cc)**\\n- `sanitizeContentLength()`: Removes content-length from CONNECT requests or when transfer-encoding:chunked is present\\n- `sanitizeHeadersWithUnderscores()`: Removes or rejects headers with underscores based on configuration\\n- `sanitizePathWithFragment()`: Strips URL fragments from paths\\n- `transformRequestHeaders()`: Applies all sanitization transformations in sequence\\n- Validates header character sets conform to RFC specifications\\n- Supports path normalization with escaped slash handling\\n\\n### HTTP/2 Specific Validation  \\n\\n**HTTP/2 Forbidden Headers (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http2_header_validator.cc)**\\n- Enforces strict validation that connection-specific headers are forbidden in HTTP/2 per RFC 9113\\n- Forbidden header list: transfer-encoding, connection, upgrade, keep-alive, proxy-connection\\n- Returns ConnectionHeaderSanitization rejection code (uhv.http2.connection_header_rejected) when these headers are detected\\n- Validates header names are lowercase (HTTP/2 requirement)\\n- Rejects headers with uppercase letters (HTTP/2 compliance)\\n- Rejects header names with underscores if configured (headers_with_underscores_action)\\n- Validates empty header names are rejected\\n\\n### Path and Query Validation\\n\\n**Path Validation (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/header_validator.cc)**\\n- `validatePathHeaderCharacters()`: Validates path contains only RFC 3986 compliant characters\\n- `sanitizeEncodedSlashes()`: Handles percent-encoded slashes (%2F, %5C) with configurable behavior\\n- `sanitizePathWithFragment()`: Removes URL fragments from paths\\n- `transformUrlPath()`: Normalizes paths and validates encoded sequences\\n- Supports disabling path normalization while still validating character sets\\n- Detects and prevents null byte injection (%00) in paths\\n- Supports configurable character sets for path compliance modes\\n\\n### HTTP/3 (QUIC) Header Validation\\n\\n**QUIC Stream Validation (source/common/quic/envoy_quic_stream.h, source/common/quic/envoy_quic_server_stream.cc)**\\n- `validateHeader()`: Per-header validation for QUIC streams using http2::adapter::HeaderValidator\\n- Validates content-length headers for QUIC protocol requirements\\n- Supports stream-specific error handling for invalid headers\\n- Configuration option: override_stream_error_on_invalid_http_message\\n- Validates header names and values against HTTP/2 semantics (QUIC uses HTTP/2 header encoding)\\n\\n**QUIC Utilities (source/common/quic/envoy_quic_utils.h)**\\n- `quicHeadersToEnvoyHeaders()`: Converts QUIC headers to Envoy format with validation\\n- Enforces max header count and size limits during conversion\\n- Supports header validator interface for custom validation\\n\\n### Header Underscore Handling\\n\\n**Underscore Sanitization (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/header_validator.cc)**\\n- `sanitizeHeadersWithUnderscores()`: Drops or rejects headers containing underscores\\n- Configurable via HeaderValidatorConfig.headers_with_underscores_action:\\n  - ALLOW: Permits underscores\\n  - DROP_HEADER: Silently removes headers with underscores\\n  - REJECT_REQUEST: Returns validation error\\n- Stats tracking for dropped headers\\n\\n### Runtime Configuration and Guards\\n\\nKey runtime guards controlling header validation behavior:\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.validate_upstream_headers`: Enables validation of upstream request headers\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_te`: Enables TE header sanitization\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.consistent_header_validation`: RFC-compliant header validation\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_http2_headers_without_nghttp2`: Header validation without nghttp2\\n- `envoy.uhv.allow_non_compliant_characters_in_path`: Compatibility mode for path characters\\n\\n### Architecture Summary\\n\\nThe header injection prevention is enforced at multiple levels:\\n\\n1. **Codec Level**: HTTP/1, HTTP/2, and HTTP/3 codecs validate headers during parsing\\n2. **Connection Manager Level**: The connection manager sanitizes internal headers and applies transformations\\n3. **Header Validator Extensions**: Pluggable header validators provide protocol-specific validation\\n4. **Utility Functions**: Shared utility functions handle common validation patterns (hostname, method, scheme)\\n5. **Header Map Level**: The base HeaderMap class validates header strings cannot contain control characters\\n\\nThis multi-layered approach ensures comprehensive protection against HTTP request header injection attacks across all supported HTTP protocols, with configurable behavior for different security and compatibility requirements.\"\n}\nEOF\ncat /workspace/answer.json\n"

headers nominated by the Connection header\\n  - Rejecting if Connection nominates x-forwarded-* headers or pseudo-headers (RFC violation)\\n  - Sanitizing the TE (Transfer-Encoding) header when nominated\\n  - Validating TE values do not exceed 256 bytes\\n  - Validates nominated headers conform to HTTP hop-by-hop semantics\\n\\n### HTTP/1.1 Specific Validation\\n\\n**Header Codec Validation (source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc)**\\n- Validates header values for invalid characters using `headerValueIsValid()`\\n- Checks header names and values conform to HTTP/1.1 semantics\\n- Validates path formatting and rejects invalid URLs\\n- Calls `sanitizeConnectionHeader()` during request header processing\\n- Detects invalid header values (non-ASCII, control characters)\\n\\n**HTTP/1 Header Validator (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http1_header_validator.cc)**\\n- `sanitizeContentLength()`: Removes content-length from CONNECT requests or when transfer-encoding:chunked is present\\n- `sanitizeHeadersWithUnderscores()`: Removes or rejects headers with underscores based on configuration\\n- `sanitizePathWithFragment()`: Strips URL fragments from paths\\n- `transformRequestHeaders()`: Applies all sanitization transformations in sequence\\n- Validates header character sets conform to RFC specifications\\n- Supports path normalization with escaped slash handling\\n\\n### HTTP/2 Specific Validation  \\n\\n**HTTP/2 Forbidden Headers (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http2_header_validator.cc)**\\n- Enforces strict validation that connection-specific headers are forbidden in HTTP/2 per RFC 9113\\n- Forbidden header list: transfer-encoding, connection, upgrade, keep-alive, proxy-connection\\n- Returns ConnectionHeaderSanitization rejection code (uhv.http2.connection_header_rejected) when these headers are detected\\n- Validates header names are lowercase (HTTP/2 requirement)\\n- Rejects headers with uppercase letters (HTTP/2 compliance)\\n- Rejects header names with underscores if configured (headers_with_underscores_action)\\n- Validates empty header names are rejected\\n\\n### Path and Query Validation\\n\\n**Path Validation (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/header_validator.cc)**\\n- `validatePathHeaderCharacters()`: Validates path contains only RFC 3986 compliant characters\\n- `sanitizeEncodedSlashes()`: Handles percent-encoded slashes (%2F, %5C) with configurable behavior\\n- `sanitizePathWithFragment()`: Removes URL fragments from paths\\n- `transformUrlPath()`: Normalizes paths and validates encoded sequences\\n- Supports disabling path normalization while still validating character sets\\n- Detects and prevents null byte injection (%00) in paths\\n- Supports configurable character sets for path compliance modes\\n\\n### HTTP/3 (QUIC) Header Validation\\n\\n**QUIC Stream Validation (source/common/quic/envoy_quic_stream.h, source/common/quic/envoy_quic_server_stream.cc)**\\n- `validateHeader()`: Per-header validation for QUIC streams using http2::adapter::HeaderValidator\\n- Validates content-length headers for QUIC protocol requirements\\n- Supports stream-specific error handling for invalid headers\\n- Configuration option: override_stream_error_on_invalid_http_message\\n- Validates header names and values against HTTP/2 semantics (QUIC uses HTTP/2 header encoding)\\n\\n**QUIC Utilities (source/common/quic/envoy_quic_utils.h)**\\n- `quicHeadersToEnvoyHeaders()`: Converts QUIC headers to Envoy format with validation\\n- Enforces max header count and size limits during conversion\\n- Supports header validator interface for custom validation\\n\\n### Header Underscore Handling\\n\\n**Underscore Sanitization (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/header_validator.cc)**\\n- `sanitizeHeadersWithUnderscores()`: Drops or rejects headers containing underscores\\n- Configurable via HeaderValidatorConfig.headers_with_underscores_action:\\n  - ALLOW: Permits underscores\\n  - DROP_HEADER: Silently removes headers with underscores\\n  - REJECT_REQUEST: Returns validation error\\n- Stats tracking for dropped headers\\n\\n### Runtime Configuration and Guards\\n\\nKey runtime guards controlling header validation behavior:\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.validate_upstream_headers`: Enables validation of upstream request headers\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_te`: Enables TE header sanitization\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.consistent_header_validation`: RFC-compliant header validation\\n- `envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_http2_headers_without_nghttp2`: Header validation without nghttp2\\n- `envoy.uhv.allow_non_compliant_characters_in_path`: Compatibility mode for path characters\\n\\n### Architecture Summary\\n\\nThe header injection prevention is enforced at multiple levels:\\n\\n1. **Codec Level**: HTTP/1, HTTP/2, and HTTP/3 codecs validate headers during parsing\\n2. **Connection Manager Level**: The connection manager sanitizes internal headers and applies transformations\\n3. **Header Validator Extensions**: Pluggable header validators provide protocol-specific validation\\n4. **Utility Functions**: Shared utility functions handle common validation patterns (hostname, method, scheme)\\n5. **Header Map Level**: The base HeaderMap class validates header strings cannot contain control characters\\n\\nThis multi-layered approach ensures comprehensive protection against HTTP request header injection attacks across all supported HTTP protocols, with configurable behavior for different security and compatibility requirements.\"\n}"
}

source/common/quic/envoy_quic_server_stream.cc)**\n- `validateHeader()`: Per-header validation for QUIC streams using http2::adapter::HeaderValidator\n- Validates content-length headers for QUIC protocol requirements\n- Supports stream-specific error handling for invalid headers\n- Configuration option: override_stream_error_on_invalid_http_message\n- Validates header names and values against parsing\n2. **Connection Manager Level**: The connection manager sanitizes internal headers and applies transformations\n3. **Header Validator Extensions**: Pluggable header validators provide validates header strings cannot contain control characters\n\nThis multi-layered approach ensures comprehensive protection against HTTP request header injection attacks across all supported HTTP
